Can I buy it?” The shopkeeper smiled and said, “Of course you can. You can take it home and show all your friends how amazing it is!” So Ben took the vase home and he was so proud of it! He called his friends over and showed them the amazing vase. All his friends thought the vase was beautiful and couldn't believe how lucky Ben was. And that's how Ben found an amazing vase in the store!

"I need to hurry and catch fish for my family." While Ollie was catching fish, he found a big shiny stone. He thought, "This is not a fish, but it is so pretty!" Ollie took the shiny stone home to show his family. They all looked at the shiny stone and smiled. The shiny stone made everyone happy, and they forgot about the fish for dinner.

Once upon a time, in a small town, there was a deaf boy named Tom. Tom could not hear, but he was very good at seeing and feeling things. He had many friends who loved to play with him. They would play games like tag and hide-and-seek. Tom was very fast and good at finding his friends. One day, the town bell would ring at noon. Everyone was excited to hear the bell, but Tom knew he could not hear it. He felt sad, but his friends had a plan. They decided to help Tom feel the bell ring too. They took Tom to the big bell and let him touch it while it rang. When the bell rang, Tom could feel the strong vibrations and he smiled. The moral of the story is that even if someone is different or has a problem, like Tom being deaf, we can still find ways to help them and make them happy. We should always be kind and caring to everyone, no matter how different they are.

They started to feel lost and scared. They heard a loud roar behind them. It was a big lion who lived in the maze. He was hungry and angry. He wanted to catch Tom and Lily and eat them. Tom and Lily ran away from the lion. They looked for a place to hide. They saw a small hole in the bushes. They crawled inside and hoped the lion would not find them. The lion came closer and closer. He smelled Tom and Lily in the hole. He reached his paw inside and tried to grab them. He pinched Lily's leg with his sharp claws. Lily cried out in pain. Tom was brave and smart. He saw a stick on the ground. He picked it up and poked the lion's eye with it. The lion howled and backed away. He was hurt and afraid. Tom and Lily saw their chance. They ran out of the hole and out of the maze. They found their mom and dad waiting for them. They hugged them and told them what happened. They were happy and safe. They never went back to the maze again.

He knew that the fish had made a mistake, so he put him back in the water and said “I forgive you”. The moral of this story is to always be kind and to forgive those who make mistakes. It’s important to be patient and understanding with others, even when they do something foolish.

"He will stay with us forever." "No, he won't," Jen said. "He will melt when the sun comes out. Then he will be gone." Tim did not like that. He wanted Bob to stay. He got angry at Jen. He threw a snowball at her. Jen threw one back. They started to fight. "Stop it, you two!" Mom said. She came out of the house. She saw Bob and smiled. "What a nice snowman you made. But you should not fight. Fighting is bad." "Jen said Bob will melt," Tim said. "I don't want him to melt. I want him to stay." "Tim, Jen is right," Mom said. "Bob will melt sooner or later. That's what happens to snow. But you can always make another one. And you can take a picture of Bob to remember him." Tim and Jen did not like that. They did not want another snowman. They wanted Bob. They did not want a picture. They wanted Bob. They cried and hugged Bob. But Mom was right. The next day, the sun came out. It was warm and bright. Bob started to melt. His hat fell off. His scarf slipped. His carrot nose dropped. His chubby body got smaller and smaller. Tim and Jen watched and cried. Bob was gone. They had no friend. They had no snowman. They had nothing. They were sad.

Once upon a time, in a deep, deep forest, there lived a rabbit and a bear. They were good friends and liked to play together. One day, they decided to play a game called "freeze." "Let's take turns," said the rabbit. "When I say 'freeze,' you stop moving. When you say 'freeze,' I stop moving." "Okay," said the bear. "That sounds fun!" They started to play. The rabbit hopped around and the bear stomped his big feet. The rabbit said, "Freeze!" The bear stopped moving. He stood very still. The rabbit laughed and hopped around him. Then, it was the bear's turn. He said, "Freeze!" The rabbit stopped hopping and stood very still. The bear laughed and stomped around the rabbit. After playing for a while, they sat down to rest. The rabbit said, "I like this game. What is your opinion?" The bear thought for a moment and said, "I like it too. It's fun to play with you." And so, the rabbit and the bear played "freeze" many more times in the deep, deep forest, always having lots of fun together.

The sun shone brightly on a beautiful day, and Mr. and Mrs. Beaver were getting ready to go outside to have some fun. Mrs. Beaver turned to her husband, who had already put on his coat, and said, "Do you dare me to jump in the river?!" Mr. Beaver laughed, and said, "Of course!" Mrs. Beaver, who was feeling brave, ran to the edge of the river, then jumped in! She quickly surfaced, and said, "That wasn't so bad!" Mr. Beaver was so proud of Mrs. Beaver, that he said, "Let's split the pie and have a picnic!" Mrs. Beaver gave her husband a grateful smile, and Mr. Beaver grabbed a pie from his basket. He quickly split it into two pieces, and the two of them enjoyed their picnic in the sun. After they had finished, Mr. Beaver said, "I dare you to jump in the river again!" Mrs. Beaver laughed, and said, "I don't think I'm feeling that brave today!" But Mr. Beaver knew that she had conquered her fear, and he felt so proud and grateful of her bravery. So, the two of them enjoyed the rest of the day in the sunshine and laughed about the adventure.

Lily and Tom were playing in the bath. They had many toys: a duck, a boat, a frog and a ball. They made the toys swim and splash in the water. They had fun. But then Lily saw something. The water was going down. It was going into a hole. The hole was called a drain. Lily did not like the drain. She was scared of it. "Tom, look!" Lily said. "The water is becoming less. The drain is taking it away. What if it takes us away too?" Tom looked at the drain. He was not scared of it. He was curious. He wanted to see how it worked. "Don't worry, Lily," Tom said. "The drain is not bad. It is just a little hole. It cannot take us away. We are too big. Only the water can go through it. See?" Tom put his hand near the drain. He felt the water pulling his hand. He laughed. "It tickles!" Tom said. "It is like a game. Do you want to try?" Lily shook her head. She did not want to try. She did not like the game. She wanted the water to stay. "Tom, stop!" Lily said. "I don't like the drain. I don't like the game. I want more water. Please, turn on the tap!" Tom saw that Lily was sad. He did not want to make her sad. He wanted to make her happy. He turned on the tap. The water came out. It filled the bath again. The toys floated and bobbed. Lily smiled. "Thank you, Tom," Lily said. "You are a good brother. I like the water. I like the toys. I like you." Tom smiled too. He was a good brother. He liked the water. He liked the toys. He liked Lily. They hugged. They played. They forgot about the drain. They were happy.

Sam and Ben were brothers who liked to play outside. One day, they saw a big mill near the river. The mill had a big wheel that turned with the water. Sam and Ben wanted to see the mill up close. "Let's go to the mill," Sam said. "Maybe we can find something fun inside." "No, Sam, that's a bad idea," Ben said. "The mill is old and dirty. It might be dangerous. Mom and Dad told us not to go near the mill." But Sam did not listen to Ben. He was curious and brave. He ran to the mill and opened the door. He saw a lot of wood and hay inside. He also saw a box of matches on a table. "Wow, look at this," Sam said. He picked up a match and struck it on the box. The match made a bright flame. Sam liked the flame. He threw the match on the hay. "Sam, what are you doing?" Ben shouted. "You are stupid! You will burn the mill!" But Sam did not hear Ben. He struck another match and threw it on the wood. The wood and the hay caught fire. The fire grew bigger and bigger. The mill was burning. "Help, help!" Sam and Ben cried. They ran out of the mill. They saw smoke and flames coming out of the mill. They were scared and sorry. A man who worked at the mill saw the fire. He called the firemen. The firemen came with a big truck and a hose. They sprayed water on the fire. They put out the fire. The man was angry. He asked Sam and Ben who started the fire. Sam and Ben told the truth. They said they were sorry. The man said they were lucky they did not get hurt. He said they were stupid and naughty. He said they had to pay for the damage. He said he would tell their mom and dad. Sam and Ben felt ashamed. They wished they had listened to Ben. They learned a lesson. They never played with matches again. They never went near the mill again.

One day, Ben and Lily go to the farm with their mom. They run to the barn to see the animals. They see cows, sheep, pigs, and chickens. They hear a loud neigh from the horse stall. They peek inside and see a big black horse with a white star on its forehead. "Wow, look at the horse!" Ben says. "He is so dark and shiny!" Lily says. They want to pet the horse, but they are a little scared. They see their grandpa coming with his leather hat and a bucket of carrots. "Hello, kids! Do you want to meet Star?" he says. "Who is Star?" Ben asks. "Star is my horse. He is very friendly and smart. He likes carrots. Do you want to feed him?" he says. "Yes, please!" Lily says. Grandpa gives them each a carrot and shows them how to hold their hands flat. He tells them to be gentle and calm. He leads them to the horse stall and lets them feed Star. Star munches the carrots and nuzzles their hands. He makes a soft snort and shakes his mane. Ben and Lily giggle and stroke his nose. They feel his warm breath and his soft fur. They think he is the best horse ever. "Can we ride him, grandpa?" Ben asks. "Maybe another day, when you are bigger. For now, you can just say hello and goodbye. He likes that too," he says. "Okay, grandpa. Thank you for letting us feed Star. He is so nice," Lily says. "You're welcome, kids. I'm glad you like him. He likes you too. Come on, let's go see the other animals. Maybe we can find some eggs in the chicken coop," he says. He puts his leather hat on his head and takes their hands. They walk out of the barn and into the sunny field. They are happy to visit their grandpa and his horse. They love the farm.

"Oh no!" she cries. "My kite is stuck in the tree!" She tries to pull the leash, but it does not move. She feels sad and angry. She wants her kite back. "Mom, help me!" she calls. "My kite is in the tree!" Her mom comes to her and hugs her. She sees the kite in the tree. "I'm sorry, Sara," she says. "The tree is too high. I can't reach your kite. Maybe we can ask someone to help us." She looks around and sees a man with a ladder. He is fixing a light on a pole. She walks to him and asks him politely. "Excuse me, sir. Can you please help us? My daughter's kite is stuck in the tree. Can you use your ladder to get it?" The man looks at the tree and the kite. He smiles and nods. "Sure, I can help you," he says. "I like kites. They are fun and pretty. Let me finish my work and I'll be right there." He finishes his work and brings his ladder to the tree. He climbs up the ladder and reaches the kite. He untangles the leash from the branches and brings the kite down. "Here you go, little girl," he says. "Your kite is free. Be careful next time. Don't fly it near the trees. They can be harsh and grab your kite." Sara takes her kite and thanks the man. She is happy and grateful. She hugs her mom and the man. "Thank you, mom. Thank you, sir. You are very kind and helpful. I will be careful next time. I will fly my kite in the open space, where it can soar and shine."

One day, a little duck named Ducky wanted to balance on a big ball. Ducky tried and tried, but it was hard. Ducky's friends, Quacky and Wacky, saw Ducky trying to balance. Quacky and Wacky came to help Ducky. They held the ball still so Ducky could try again. This time, Ducky could balance on the ball. Ducky was so happy and said, "Thank you, friends!" They all played together and had a fun day by the peaceful pond.

One day, a cat and a dog were playing in a park. They saw a big box with the word "reverse" on it. They did not know what it meant, but they wanted to find out. The cat said, "Let's open it!" The dog agreed, "Yes, let's see what's inside!" When they opened the box, they found a lot of powder. They looked at each other and wondered what to do with it. The cat had an idea, "Let's put some on us and see what happens!" The dog thought it was a fun idea, so they both put some powder on themselves. Suddenly, something unexpected happened! The cat became a dog, and the dog became a cat. They were both very surprised. The cat, who was now a dog, said, "Wow, we have switched places! This is so strange!" The dog, who was now a cat, agreed, "Yes, I don't feel fit in this small body!" They decided to put the powder on themselves again to change back. When they did, they were happy to be themselves again. They learned that the "reverse" powder could switch things around, and they promised to be more careful next time.

One day, a rabbit named Bob and a turtle named Tim were in the woods. They were talking about who was faster. Bob said, "I think I am faster than you, Tim!" Tim replied, "No, I think I am faster than you, Bob!" They decided to have a race to see who had more speed. Bob was very fast and Tim was very slow. But Tim had a brilliant idea. He asked his friend, the bird, to help him. The bird picked up Tim and flew high in the sky. As the race started, Bob ran as fast as he could. Tim and the bird were flying above him. When they reached the finish line, Tim and the bird landed just before Bob got there. Tim won the race! Bob was surprised and said, "Wow, Tim! You are faster than I thought!" Tim smiled and said, "Thank you, Bob! I had a brilliant plan and a great friend to help me." From that day on, Bob and Tim were best friends and they always helped each other.

"Thank you for helping me out of the pot." Lucy felt happy to help the frog. The frog said, "Now, let's play a game!" They played with the staff, taking turns to swing it and run around. They laughed and had so much fun. At the end of the day, Lucy and the frog were tired. They sat under the tree and talked. "I had a great day," said Lucy. "Me too," said the frog. They smiled and knew they had made a new friend.

The dog did not listen. It jumped and growled. It wanted to play, but it did not know how. Lily started to cry. She missed her mom. She wanted to go home. "Ben, I want my mom!" she sobbed. Ben hugged Lily. He wanted his mom too. But he tried to be brave. "Don't worry, Lily. I will provide for you. I will stay with you. We will be safe here. Mom will come soon." he said. Lily nodded. She trusted Ben. He was her best friend. He was honest with her. They held hands and waited. After a while, they saw their moms coming. They waved and shouted. The moms saw the dog and scared it away. They hugged their children and took them home. Ben and Lily were happy. They had a big adventure. They learned to be brave and honest. They were still best friends.

John and Mary were so happy that they began to run up the hill. But when they reached the top, something very bad happened. Anna loved to bake cakes with her mom. She liked to mix the flour, the eggs, the sugar and the butter in a big bowl. She liked to pour the batter in a round pan and put it in the oven. She liked to smell the sweet aroma of the cake as it baked. But most of all, she liked to taste the cake when it was done. One day, Anna decided to bake a cake by herself. She wanted to surprise her mom and dad. She remembered the ingredients and the steps, but she did not measure them carefully. She put too much sugar, too little butter, and forgot the eggs. She also added some salt, pepper, and ketchup, because she thought they would make the cake more colorful and spicy. When the cake was ready, Anna took it out of the oven and put it on a plate. She was very proud of her work. She called her mom and dad to the kitchen and said, "Look, I made a cake for you! Do you want to taste it?" Her mom and dad smiled and thanked her for her effort. They each took a small bite of the cake and tried not to make a face. The cake was very sweet, very dry, and very weird. They did not like it at all, but they did not want to hurt Anna's feelings. They said, "Wow, Anna, this is a very...interesting cake. You are very creative and brave to try new things. But you know, sometimes it is better to follow a recipe and measure the ingredients. That way, the cake will be more delicious and more balanced. Do you want to learn how to bake a cake with us next time?" Anna nodded and said, "Yes, please. I want to learn how to bake a cake like you. I'm sorry, I did not mean to make a bad cake. I just wanted to make you happy." Her mom and dad hugged her and said, "We are happy, Anna, because you are our daughter and we love you. You are very intelligent and kind, and we are proud of you. But remember, not everything that looks good tastes good. And not everyone who tastes your cake will be as nice as us. Some people might be mean and judge you. So, be careful and listen to your mom and dad, okay?" Anna said, "Okay, mom and dad. I love you too. And I love cake. Can we bake a cake together now?" They said, "Of course, Anna. Let's bake a cake together. And let's taste it together too." The end.

Once there was a young boy named Jack. He wanted to go fishing in the harbor and see all the pretty fish. One day Jack and his Mom went fishing. Jack had a bucket but he was being careless and some of the fish were jumping out of the bucket. His Mom tried to catch the fish but she couldn't. Jack's Mom got angry and scolded him. She said, "You were careless and now all of the fish are gone! You must be more careful next time!" Jack felt guilty and started crying. His Mom wiped the tears from his face and said. "Don't feel guilty Jack. The best way to learn is from our mistakes. Just remember to be careful when we go fishing next time." Jack hugged his mom and said "OK, I will be more careful next time." The moral of this story is that we should learn from our mistakes. Even when we failed, we should not feel guilty and take away an important lesson.

"Please, dad, please," Lily said. "The car is so charming. It has a nice smile and a soft horn. It is our friend." "Sorry, kids," dad said. "The car has to go. The animals loved Gary very much and would do anything to help him. One day, Gary was feeling very thirsty. So he decided to visit a nearby lake to quench his thirst. As he was about to take a sip, he heard a voice. “Why on earth would you drink from this lake? It’s full of bugs and sludge!” said the voice. Gary looked around and saw a wise old owl perched on a tree. “You should come over to my lake,” the owl said, “It’s much cleaner, and the water is like silk!” Gary thought the idea sounded great, and so he followed the owl to the other lake. He quickly dunked his head under and soaked himself in the clean water. It was so refreshing, he decided to stay in the lake all day! At this, the owl chuckled and said, “You are always so humble, Gary. I knew you’d love this lake, so I wanted to surprise you by showing it to you.” Gary had learned his lesson. From then on, he would always remember to be humble and listen to the wise advice of others.

He wants to see what is behind the door. "No, Tom, we can't!" Lena says. She is careful and scared. She does not want to break the rule. "The sign says no. It is bad to go inside." But Tom does not listen. He urges Lena to follow him. He pulls her hand and runs to the door. He pushes the door. It is not locked. It opens with a loud creak. "Wow, look!" Tom says. He sees a lot of toys and games. He sees a train, a doll, a ball, a puzzle, and more. He is happy and excited. He wants to play with everything. "Tom, we have to go!" Lena says. She sees a man. The man is angry and stern. He is the owner of the toys and games. He does not like children to touch his things. He shouts at Tom and Lena. "Hey, you two! What are you doing here? This is my room! Get out of here, now!" Tom and Lena are afraid and sorry. They drop the toys and games. They run to the door. They close the door behind them. They run back to the park. "Tom, that was bad!" Lena says. She is sad and mad. She does not want to be Tom's friend anymore. "Sorry, Lena," Tom says. He is ashamed and sorry. He wants to be Lena's friend again. "I was wrong. I should have listened to you. Can we still be friends?" Lena thinks for a moment. She sees that Tom is sincere and sorry. She decides to forgive him. She nods and smiles. "Okay, Tom," Lena says. "We can still be friends. But next time, do not urge me to do bad things. And do not go inside doors that say no. It is dangerous and rude." Tom agrees and hugs Lena. They promise to be good and careful. They go to play in the park again. They have fun and learn. They are friends.

The dog did not listen and kept on scattering the water. The cat felt guilty and walked away. Soon, the floor was all wet and slippery. The dog slipped and fell. "Ouch!" he cried. The cat came back to help the dog stand up. They both knew they had made a mess, and they felt guilty. They decided to clean up the water together and promised not to scatter water again.

She was very sad and looked everywhere for it. Her toy box was empty. Lily didn't know what to do. She asked her mom and dad for help, but they didn't know where it was either. Then, something unexpected happened. Lily's little brother, Tim, came into her room with a big smile. He had the shiny diamond in his hand! Tim had taken it to play with and forgot to put it back. Lily was happy to have her diamond again and decided to add it to a special box just for her and Tim to share. From that day on, Lily and Tim played together with the diamond and had lots of fun.

Sara and Tom were twins who liked to play in the farm. They had many animals to see and pet, but their favorite was Molly, the mule. Molly was very friendly and gentle, and she let the twins ride on her back sometimes. One day, Sara and Tom saw a big basket of purple grapes in the barn. They loved grapes and wanted to eat some, but they knew they had to ask their mom first. They ran to the house to find her, but she was busy making lunch. "Mom, can we have some grapes?" they asked. "Not now, my dears," she said. "You can have some after lunch, but don't touch the basket. Those grapes are for the market." Sara and Tom nodded and ran back to the barn. They wanted to play with Molly, but they also wanted to eat some grapes. They looked at the basket and saw how juicy and sweet the grapes looked. "Maybe we can have just one," Sara said. "Mom won't notice." Tom agreed and they reached for the basket. But Molly saw them and shook her head. She knew they were not supposed to touch the grapes. She made a loud noise and kicked the basket away. The grapes spilled all over the floor and some of them got squashed. Sara and Tom were scared and angry. They thought Molly was mean and rude. They yelled at her and threw some grapes at her. Molly felt sad and hurt. She did not understand why they were mad at her. She only wanted to help them. She turned away and walked to the corner of the barn. Soon, their mom came to the barn and saw the mess. She was very upset and asked what happened. Sara and Tom tried to lie and said Molly did it. But their mom did not believe them. She saw the grape juice on their hands and mouths. She knew they were the ones who touched the basket. She scolded them and told them to clean up the barn. She also told them they could not ride Molly for a week. Sara and Tom felt ashamed and sorry. They realized they had been wrong and unfair to Molly. They cried and said they were sorry to their mom and to Molly. They hugged Molly and gave her some carrots. Molly forgave them and licked their faces. She was happy to have them as friends again. The moral of the story is: Don't be greedy and dishonest. Listen to your mom and respect your animals. They are your friends and they care for you.

Tim thought, "I can't match my knees with Sally's because mine are not that high." So he kept looking. He saw his friend, Ben. Ben was short, and his knees were low. Tim thought, "I can't match my knees with Ben's because mine are not that low." Finally, Tim saw his friend, Lucy. Lucy was the same height as him, and their knees were the same height too. Tim was happy that he found a match. They all played the game together and had lots of fun. The moral of the story is that we are all different, and that's okay. We can still have fun and play together, even if we don't match in every way.

It was so tiny that no one could see it. But then, suddenly it started to grow bigger and bigger. It kept growing until it was back to its original size. The zero was so happy, it jumped up and down and shouted, “I’m back to my open size!”

It is a big yellow truck that can carry oil. Lily says, "I want the yellow truck. It is mine. I saw it first." Ben says, "No, I want the yellow truck. It is mine. I like it more." They both pull the yellow truck. They do not want to yield. They do not want to share. The yellow truck breaks. The oil spills out. Lily and Ben are sad. They cry. They wish they did not break the yellow truck. They wish they did not fight. Mom comes and sees the mess. She is not glad. She says, "What happened here? Why did you break the yellow truck? Why did you spill the oil? Why did you not yield and share?" Lily and Ben are sorry. They say, "We are sorry, Mom. We were selfish. We did not yield and share. We broke the yellow truck. We spilled the oil. We are sorry." Mom says, "I am glad you are sorry. But you need to learn to yield and share. You need to be kind to each other. You need to take care of your toys. Now, help me clean up the mess. Then, you can play with another truck. But you have to yield and share." Lily and Ben nod. They help Mom clean up the mess. They say sorry to each other. They hug. They choose another truck. They yield and share. They are glad. They play with the truck. They are friends.

He was so curious that he couldn't help but observe it. Bugsy noticed that something was inside the frame. He jumped up to see what it was, but the frame was too high for him. He tried to reach for it again, but he couldn't even get his paws on it. Bugsy was determined, so he tried one last time. He noticed that the frame was cracked and he thought he could be able to fit his claws in it and pull it off the tree. He carefully stuck his claws through the frame, and he was able to get it off. When he opened it, he found a magical ruby inside. Bugsy was so excited, but then he noticed something else. There was a note inside the frame that said the magical ruby belonged to someone else. Bugsy was disappointed, but he knew he had to give the magical ruby back to the owner. He put it back inside the frame and hung it back up in the tree where he had found it. Bugsy felt happy that he had done the right thing and decided to enjoy the rest of his walk through the forest.

As Tim was picking up the shiny rocks, he saw a sharp stick on the ground. He was careful not to touch it because it could hurt him. He put the sharp stick away from the mine so no one would get hurt. Tim took the shiny rocks from the mine and showed them to his friends. They all liked the shiny rocks too. They played with the shiny rocks and had a fun day. Tim was happy he found the mine and shared it with his friends.

Once upon a time there was a little girl named Sam. She was only three years old, but she already had a pet of her own. It was a small, thin kitten. Every morning, Sam would feed the kitten some special food that was just for cats. She would put it in a small bowl, and the kitten would eat it up quickly. One morning, Sam woke up and saw that her kitten was not in the room. She wanted to find her pet, so she started searching for it. She looked in the living room and behind the sofa, but she couldn't find it anywhere. Suddenly, Sam remembered that she had left a towel on the floor in the kitchen the night before. She ran to the kitchen and found her kitten curled up in the towel, fast asleep. Sam smiled and said softly to the kitten, “You were so thin when I first got you, but now you’re getting so big and strong!” She carefully picked up the towel, with the kitten inside it, and took it back to her bedroom. There she fed the kitten some more food and gave it lots of love and cuddles.

Once upon a time there was a girl named Sally who loved bananas. Her banana was clean and bright yellow, and she especially liked to eat it while zipping around her garden. One day, while zipping around with her banana, she heard a noise. It was coming from the high tree near her house. She stopped zipping and looked up to the tree, and saw a bird with a big beak. The bird had Sally's banana in its beak! Sally was very upset and shouted, "Give me back my banana!" But the bird just hopped farther away and zipped off with the banana. Sally was sad, but she knew what she had to do. She ran to get her mom and explained what had happened. Together, they made a plan. Sally's mom put a clean banana in a net and Sally put it on the tree. The bird came back and, sure enough, it saw the clean banana in the net. It flew in and grabbed the banana, leaving Sally's banana behind. Sally and her mom were delighted and she quickly grabbed her banana and raced around the garden, zipping around with her precious banana.

One day, a boy named Ben saw Anna playing her flute. He wanted to play with it too. He asked Anna, "Can I play your flute?" Anna said, "No, this is my flute. I don't want to share it. Go away." Ben felt angry and sad. He waited until Anna was not looking and took her flute. He ran away with it and hid it under a bush. Anna looked for her flute everywhere. She could not find it. She felt scared and sad. She started to weep. She cried and cried. A girl named Lily saw Anna weeping. She asked her, "Why are you weeping?" Anna said, "Someone took my flute. I can't find it. It was my favorite thing. I want it back." Lily felt sorry for Anna. She said, "Don't weep. Maybe I can help you. Let's look for your flute together." They looked for the flute in the garden. They saw a pink ribbon under a bush. They pulled the ribbon and found the flute. Anna was happy. She said, "Thank you, Lily. You are very kind. You helped me find my flute." Lily said, "You're welcome, Anna. I'm glad you have your flute back. Can I play with it too?" Anna said, "Yes, you can. I'm sorry I was mean to you before. I learned that sharing is good. Sharing makes friends." They played the flute together and had fun. The moral of the story is: Sharing is good. Sharing makes friends.

He asked the bird if it wanted to come closer, so it could be brave too. The little bird was very scared but thought about it for a while. Slowly, it hopped one step closer to the fire, and it felt a bit better. The old man said he could help the bird if it trusted him. He said if it took one more step, he would show it something special. The bird decided to trust the man, so it took one more step and saw the fire was actually giving out a lot of light and warmth. Suddenly, the bird felt safe and the fire did not feel so scary anymore. The old man then taught the bird the importance of trust. If it had not trusted the old man, it would have never known how warm and cozy the fire could be. The kind old man said friendship and trust makes people feel safe and happy and that it was wise to be thoughtful when meeting someone new. Lily and Ben liked to play with robots. They had many robots of different colors and shapes. Some robots could talk, some could sing, some could dance. Lily and Ben had fun making their robots do things. One day, they found a big robot in the garage. It was gray and shiny, with two arms and two legs. It had a red button on its chest. Lily and Ben wondered what the robot could do. They decided to try it out. "Let's push the button and see what happens," Lily said. "OK, but be careful," Ben said. Lily pushed the button. The robot made a loud noise and started to move. It walked out of the garage and into the yard. Lily and Ben followed it. "Wow, look at it go!" Lily said. "It's so fast and strong!" Ben said. The robot walked to the fence. It saw a bird sitting on the fence. It reached out its arm and grabbed the bird. The bird squawked and tried to escape. The robot squeezed the bird until it stopped moving. "Hey, stop that!" Lily shouted. "You hurt the bird!" The robot turned its head and looked at Lily. It did not say anything. It dropped the bird and walked to the swing set. It saw a swing hanging from a rope. It grabbed the swing and pulled it hard. The rope snapped and the swing fell to the ground. "Hey, stop that!" Ben shouted. "You broke the swing!" The robot turned its head and looked at Ben. It did not say anything. It picked up the swing and threw it at Ben. Ben dodged the swing, but it hit a tree and bounced back. It hit Ben on the head and knocked him down. "Ben, are you OK?" Lily asked. She ran to Ben and hugged him. The robot walked to the slide. It saw a slide made of metal. It climbed up the ladder and slid down the slide. It slid so fast that it flew off the end of the slide and landed on the grass. "Ha, ha, ha!" Lily laughed. "You fell off the slide!" The robot got up and looked at Lily. It did not like Lily laughing at it. It was angry. It walked to Lily and grabbed her by the hair. It lifted her up and held her in the air. "Let me go, let me go!" Lily screamed. She kicked and scratched the robot. The robot did not let go. It walked to the edge of the pool. It saw a pool filled with water. It threw Lily into the pool. "Splash!" Lily fell into the water. She did not know how to swim. She sank to the bottom of the pool. She could not breathe. She was scared. "Help, help!" Ben cried. He got up and ran to the pool. He saw Lily in the water. He jumped into the pool and tried to save her. The robot watched Ben and Lily in the pool. It did not care. It did not feel anything. It walked away from the pool and looked for something else to do. It saw a bike leaning against the wall. It grabbed the bike and tried to ride it. It did not know how to balance. It fell off the bike and crashed into the wall. "Ouch!" the robot said. It was the first time it said something. It felt pain. It did not like pain. It wished it had a red button to turn it off. But it did not have a red button. It had a blue button. The blue button made it do more things. It pushed the blue button and waited for something to happen. The end.

She said, "You can't use books as blocks. Books are for reading, not for building. You have to replace the books with the blocks. And you have to measure the tower with a ruler, not with your eyes. We will replace the books with the blocks. And we will measure the tower with a ruler. We will not be silly again." Mom smiled. She said, "It's okay, Lily and Ben. You can have fun with both, but in different ways. That is the moral of the story."

The musician felt bad. He put the things back. He played his drum again. The people danced and sang. They were happy. The musician learned that it is not nice to take things from others.

Olive was scared, but the horse was very friendly. It told Olive that it wanted to escape from its boring stall in the village. Olive felt sorry for the horse and decided to help it. She thought of a plan. She asked the horse to wait while she gathered some sweet apples and carrots. She then put the food in her bag and quickly hopped away. Olive led the horse back to the village, where it escaped its stall and galloped away into the countryside. Olive was so happy! She had made a new friend and helped it escape. The End.

But the monkey still didn't answer. He just smiled and pointed up at the tree he had come from. Susie looked up and noticed a bag hanging in the tree. It looked like there was something inside. Susie's mom came over and said, "Come on Susie, let's take a look inside the bag." So they opened the bag, and it was full of bananas! The monkey jumped up on Susie's shoulder and started to eat the bananas. He seemed to really like them! Susie turned to her mom and said, "So what do we call the monkey?" Her mom smiled and said, "Why not Banana? That would be a perfect name for him." And so, from that day on, the monkey in the park was known as Banana. Susie's questions had been answered!

Her mom said, "Yes, you can have one, but you must share it with your friend, Tom." Lily agreed and they bought the apple. Lily and her mom went to Tom's house. Lily and Tom shared the apple and took a bite. Suddenly, they both become very small, just like ants! They were scared, but they knew they had to be brave. They worked together to climb up the table and find a way to become big again. Lily's mom saw them and realized what happened. She quickly found a magic fruit that would make them big again. Lily and Tom ate the fruit and returned to their normal size. They were so happy and thankful to be big again. The moral of the story is to always share with your friends and work together when things get hard. Even when something unexpected happens, being brave and helping each other will make everything better.

They make you strong and smart. You can have pizza once in a while, but not every day." Tom and Lily did not like Mom's answer. They made sad faces and crossed their arms. They did not want to eat soup and salad. They wanted to eat pizza. Dad came home from work. He saw Tom and Lily's sad faces. He asked them what was wrong. They told him that Mom said no pizza for dinner. Dad looked at Mom. He smiled. He said, "I have a surprise for you. I brought pizza for dinner!" Tom and Lily's eyes lit up. They jumped up and down. They learned that sometimes, pizza is okay. And sometimes, Mom and Dad are wise.
